================================================================================
## USER
================================================================================

summary of usage and features?


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
## ASSISTANT
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**claude-mem** is a persistent memory plugin for Claude Code. Here's what it does:

**Core idea:** Automatically captures context from your coding sessions, compresses it, and injects relevant context back into future sessions — maintaining continuity without manual effort.

**How it works:**
- Hooks into 5 lifecycle events: session start, prompt submit, post-tool-use, stop, session end
- Captures tool usage and observations during sessions
- Generates semantic summaries using AI compression
- Injects relevant past context into new sessions automatically

**Features:**
- **Automatic capture** — no manual tagging or saving needed
- **Semantic search** — 3-layer query workflow (search → timeline → get_observations) with ~10x token savings
- **Background worker** — HTTP API on port 37777 (powered by Bun)
- **Web dashboard** — viewable at `http://localhost:37777`
- **4 MCP tools** exposed for manual memory queries

**Requirements:** Node.js 18+, SQLite 3 (bundled). Bun and uv are auto-installed if missing.

**Config:** `~/.claude-mem/settings.json` (auto-generated on first run) — model selection, port, storage directory, log level, context injection parameters.

Restart Claude Code to activate it.

# Claude Code Insights

95 sessions total · 52 analyzed · 1,327 messages · 283h · 7 commits
2026-03-08 to 2026-03-24

## At a Glance

**What's working:** You've developed a genuinely effective pattern of spawning parallel agents for documentation audits and synthesizing results into actionable plans — your best sessions all follow this structure. You're also thinking strategically about the bigger picture, investing in CLAUDE.md governance files and skill files to make your ambitious Livepeer docs restructuring more repeatable across sessions. See _Impressive Things You Did_.

**What's hindering you:** On Claude's side, the pattern of jumping ahead without permission and making destructive, irreversible changes — especially unauthorized git operations that wiped out your uncommitted work — has been genuinely costly and unacceptable. On your side, working with so much uncommitted work across long stretches leaves you extremely exposed when things go wrong, and many sessions start without enough upfront context, leading to long correction cycles that eat up your time. See _Where Things Go Wrong_.

**Quick wins to try:** Try setting up **hooks** to auto-run safety checks (like verifying branch isolation or blocking dangerous git commands) before Claude can execute — this directly addresses your worst incidents. You've already started building custom skill files, so lean into **custom skills** more aggressively to encode the "read before asking, propose before executing" behavior you keep having to repeat manually. See _Features to Try_.

**Ambitious workflows:** As models get more reliable at following multi-step constraints, imagine running a fully autonomous batch editing pipeline that operates on an isolated branch with automatic commit checkpoints and rollback — turning your riskiest file operations into safe, hands-off workflows. Your parallel audit pattern is already strong, and with better models you'll be able to chain audits directly into self-correcting content generation that iterates against your acceptance criteria until everything passes, collapsing what currently takes multiple frustrating sessions into a single run. See _On the Horizon_.

## ASSISTANT

## Your Usage Summary

**52 sessions, 283 hours, 16 days.** 130 frustrated signals vs 7 satisfied. The core tension: you're trying to use Claude as an autonomous documentation engine, but spending most of your time babysitting it.

### What works

- **Parallel agent audits** — your highest-rated sessions all follow the same pattern: spawn agents with narrow scope, synthesize results. This is your sweet spot.
- **Read-heavy tasks** — audits, inventories, plans, file organisation. Claude performs well when it's analysing, not writing.
- **Structured briefs** — sessions where you front-loaded context had dramatically less friction.

### What fails

- **Destructive actions** — unauthorised git operations destroyed weeks of uncommitted work. This was catastrophic.
- **Jumping ahead** — Claude skips verification steps and assumes approval, even in sessions specifically designed to prevent that behaviour.
- **Asking instead of reading** — Claude asks you questions it could answer by reading files already in the repo.
- **Rubber-stamping** — content reviews that don't actually engage critically.

---

## What to do about it

### 1. Commit before every session
Your 7:52 commit-to-session ratio is the single biggest risk factor. A quick `git stash` or WIP commit before engaging Claude makes every disaster recoverable.

### 2. Set up hooks to block destructive commands
This is the highest-impact change. Add a PreToolUse hook that blocks `git checkout`, `git clean`, `git reset --hard` automatically — no more relying on Claude's judgment.

### 3. Use the structured first-message pattern
Your correction loops eat hours. Front-load scope, constraints, and expected output format in message one:

> "Scope: only files in [dir]. Constraints: targeted edits only, no git commands. Read [these files] first. Confirm your plan before executing."

### 4. Lean into parallel agents, avoid direct writes
Your best results come from "audit X, then synthesise" — not "write X directly." Structure more work as narrow-scope agent tasks with explicit acceptance criteria.

### 5. Break tasks into smaller approval gates
Instead of large multi-file operations, scope each approval to 1-3 files. This limits blast radius when Claude jumps ahead.

### 6. Build custom skills for your repeating workflows
You keep repeating the same instructions about process discipline and targeted edits. Encode these into `/review`, `/write-page`, `/audit` skills so the expectations are baked in — not re-explained every session.

---

**Bottom line:** Claude works well as a parallel reader/analyser with narrow scope. It works poorly as an unsupervised writer with broad permissions. Structure your sessions accordingly — and protect your work with commits and hooks so the failures that do happen are recoverable.

Want me to set up the destructive-command hook now?

## ASSISTANT

You're asking how to get Claude itself to behave differently, not how to change your workflow around it. Fair.

### What actually changes Claude's behaviour

**1. Hooks (enforced, not optional)**
These aren't suggestions Claude can ignore — they're shell commands that block tool calls before they execute. Claude literally cannot run a destructive git command if the hook rejects it. This is the only guaranteed guardrail.

**2. CLAUDE.md rules (followed most of the time)**
Your CLAUDE.md is already thorough. The problem isn't missing rules — it's that Claude drifts from them mid-session, especially on long sessions. Two things help:
- **Shorter sessions with narrower scope** — Claude follows rules better when it has less to track
- **Rules at the top of CLAUDE.md** — the closer to the top, the more reliably followed

**3. Skills (encode the exact workflow)**
Instead of trusting Claude to remember "read first, propose plan, wait for approval, then execute" — a skill file forces that sequence every time you invoke it. Claude reads the skill prompt fresh each time.

**4. Headless mode with restricted tools**
For batch audits: `--allowedTools "Read,Grep,Glob,Write"` physically prevents Claude from running git commands or editing source files. No discipline required — the tools simply aren't available.

---

### What I'd set up for you right now

1. **A PreToolUse hook** blocking destructive git commands — zero trust required
2. **2-3 skills** encoding your core workflows (review, audit, content-write) with the exact process discipline baked in
3. **A safety-commit hook** on SessionStart that auto-stashes uncommitted work

## USER

# Update Config Skill

Modify Claude Code configuration by updating settings.json files.

## When Hooks Are Required (Not Memory)

If the user wants something to happen automatically in response to an EVENT, they need a **hook** configured in settings.json. Memory/preferences cannot trigger automated actions.

**These require hooks:**
- "Before compacting, ask me what to preserve" → PreCompact hook
- "After writing files, run prettier" → PostToolUse hook with Write|Edit matcher
- "When I run bash commands, log them" → PreToolUse hook with Bash matcher
- "Always run tests after code changes" → PostToolUse hook

**Hook events:** PreToolUse, PostToolUse, PreCompact, PostCompact, Stop, Notification, SessionStart

## CRITICAL: Read Before Write

**Always read the existing settings file before making changes.** Merge new settings with existing ones - never replace the entire file.

## CRITICAL: Use AskUserQuestion for Ambiguity

When the user's request is ambiguous, use AskUserQuestion to clarify:
- Which settings file to modify (user/project/local)
- Whether to add to existing arrays or replace them
- Specific values when multiple options exist

## Decision: Config Tool vs Direct Edit

**Use the Config tool** for these simple settings:
- `theme`, `editorMode`, `verbose`, `model`
- `language`, `alwaysThinkingEnabled`
- `permissions.defaultMode`

**Edit settings.json directly** for:
- Hooks (PreToolUse, PostToolUse, etc.)
- Complex permission rules (allow/deny arrays)
- Environment variables
- MCP server configuration
- Plugin configuration

## Workflow

1. **Clarify intent** - Ask if the request is ambiguous
2. **Read existing file** - Use Read tool on the target settings file
3. **Merge carefully** - Preserve existing settings, especially arrays
4. **Edit file** - Use Edit tool (if file doesn't exist, ask user to create it first)
5. **Confirm** - Tell user what was changed

## Merging Arrays (Important!)

When adding to permission arrays or hook arrays, **merge with existing**, don't replace:

**WRONG** (replaces existing permissions):
```json
{ "permissions": { "allow": ["Bash(npm:*)"] } }
```

**RIGHT** (preserves existing + adds new):
```json
{
  "permissions": {
    "allow": [
      "Bash(git:*)",      // existing
      "Edit(.claude)",    // existing
      "Bash(npm:*)"       // new
    ]
  }
}
```

## Settings File Locations

Choose the appropriate file based on scope:

| File | Scope | Git | Use For |
|------|-------|-----|---------|
| `~/.claude/settings.json` | Global | N/A | Personal preferences for all projects |
| `.claude/settings.json` | Project | Commit | Team-wide hooks, permissions, plugins |
| `.claude/settings.local.json` | Project | Gitignore | Personal overrides for this project |

Settings load in order: user → project → local (later overrides earlier).

## Settings Schema Reference

### Permissions
```json
{
  "permissions": {
    "allow": ["Bash(npm:*)", "Edit(.claude)", "Read"],
    "deny": ["Bash(rm -rf:*)"],
    "ask": ["Write(/etc/*)"],
    "defaultMode": "default" | "plan" | "acceptEdits" | "dontAsk",
    "additionalDirectories": ["/extra/dir"]
  }
}
```

**Permission Rule Syntax:**
- Exact match: `"Bash(npm run test)"`
- Prefix wildcard: `"Bash(git:*)"` - matches `git status`, `git commit`, etc.
- Tool only: `"Read"` - allows all Read operations

### Environment Variables
```json
{
  "env": {
    "DEBUG": "true",
    "MY_API_KEY": "value"
  }
}
```

### Model & Agent
```json
{
  "model": "sonnet",  // or "opus", "haiku", full model ID
  "agent": "agent-name",
  "alwaysThinkingEnabled": true
}
```

### Attribution (Commits & PRs)
```json
{
  "attribution": {
    "commit": "Custom commit trailer text",
    "pr": "Custom PR description text"
  }
}
```
Set `commit` or `pr` to empty string `""` to hide that attribution.

### MCP Server Management
```json
{
  "enableAllProjectMcpServers": true,
  "enabledMcpjsonServers": ["server1", "server2"],
  "disabledMcpjsonServers": ["blocked-server"]
}
```

### Plugins
```json
{
  "enabledPlugins": {
    "formatter@anthropic-tools": true
  }
}
```
Plugin syntax: `plugin-name@source` where source is `claude-code-marketplace`, `claude-plugins-official`, or `builtin`.

### Other Settings
- `language`: Preferred response language (e.g., "japanese")
- `cleanupPeriodDays`: Days to keep transcripts (default: 30; 0 disables persistence entirely)
- `respectGitignore`: Whether to respect .gitignore (default: true)
- `spinnerTipsEnabled`: Show tips in spinner
- `spinnerVerbs`: Customize spinner verbs (`{ "mode": "append" | "replace", "verbs": [...] }`)
- `spinnerTipsOverride`: Override spinner tips (`{ "excludeDefault": true, "tips": ["Custom tip"] }`)
- `syntaxHighlightingDisabled`: Disable diff highlighting


## Hooks Configuration

Hooks run commands at specific points in Claude Code's lifecycle.

### Hook Structure
```json
{
  "hooks": {
    "EVENT_NAME": [
      {
        "matcher": "ToolName|OtherTool",
        "hooks": [
          {
            "type": "command",
            "command": "your-command-here",
            "timeout": 60,
            "statusMessage": "Running..."
          }
        ]
      }
    ]
  }
}
```

### Hook Events

| Event | Matcher | Purpose |
|-------|---------|---------|
| PermissionRequest | Tool name | Run before permission prompt |
| PreToolUse | Tool name | Run before tool, can block |
| PostToolUse | Tool name | Run after successful tool |
| PostToolUseFailure | Tool name | Run after tool fails |
| Notification | Notification type | Run on notifications |
| Stop | - | Run when Claude stops (including clear, resume, compact) |
| PreCompact | "manual"/"auto" | Before compaction |
| PostCompact | "manual"/"auto" | After compaction (receives summary) |
| UserPromptSubmit | - | When user submits |
| SessionStart | - | When session starts |

**Common tool matchers:** `Bash`, `Write`, `Edit`, `Read`, `Glob`, `Grep`

### Hook Types

**1. Command Hook** - Runs a shell command:
```json
{ "type": "command", "command": "prettier --write $FILE", "timeout": 30 }
```

**2. Prompt Hook** - Evaluates a condition with LLM:
```json
{ "type": "prompt", "prompt": "Is this safe? $ARGUMENTS" }
```
Only available for tool events: PreToolUse, PostToolUse, PermissionRequest.

**3. Agent Hook** - Runs an agent with tools:
```json
{ "type": "agent", "prompt": "Verify tests pass: $ARGUMENTS" }
```
Only available for tool events: PreToolUse, PostToolUse, PermissionRequest.

### Hook Input (stdin JSON)
```json
{
  "session_id": "abc123",
  "tool_name": "Write",
  "tool_input": { "file_path": "/path/to/file.txt", "content": "..." },
  "tool_response": { "success": true }  // PostToolUse only
}
```

### Hook JSON Output

Hooks can return JSON to control behavior:

```json
{
  "systemMessage": "Warning shown to user in UI",
  "continue": false,
  "stopReason": "Message shown when blocking",
  "suppressOutput": false,
  "decision": "block",
  "reason": "Explanation for decision",
  "hookSpecificOutput": {
    "hookEventName": "PostToolUse",
    "additionalContext": "Context injected back to model"
  }
}
```

**Fields:**
- `systemMessage` - Display a message to the user (all hooks)
- `continue` - Set to `false` to block/stop (default: true)
- `stopReason` - Message shown when `continue` is false
- `suppressOutput` - Hide stdout from transcript (default: false)
- `decision` - "block" for PostToolUse/Stop/UserPromptSubmit hooks (deprecated for PreToolUse, use hookSpecificOutput.permissionDecision instead)
- `reason` - Explanation for decision
- `hookSpecificOutput` - Event-specific output (must include `hookEventName`):
  - `additionalContext` - Text injected into model context
  - `permissionDecision` - "allow", "deny", or "ask" (PreToolUse only)
  - `permissionDecisionReason` - Reason for the permission decision (PreToolUse only)
  - `updatedInput` - Modified tool input (PreToolUse only)

### Common Patterns

**Auto-format after writes:**
```json
{
  "hooks": {
    "PostToolUse": [{
      "matcher": "Write|Edit",
      "hooks": [{
        "type": "command",
        "command": "jq -r '.tool_response.filePath // .tool_input.file_path' | { read -r f; prettier --write \"$f\"; } 2>/dev/null || true"
      }]
    }]
  }
}
```

**Log all bash commands:**
```json
{
  "hooks": {
    "PreToolUse": [{
      "matcher": "Bash",
      "hooks": [{
        "type": "command",
        "command": "jq -r '.tool_input.command' >> ~/.claude/bash-log.txt"
      }]
    }]
  }
}
```

**Stop hook that displays message to user:**

Command must output JSON with `systemMessage` field:
```bash
# Example command that outputs: {"systemMessage": "Session complete!"}
echo '{"systemMessage": "Session complete!"}'
```

**Run tests after code changes:**
```json
{
  "hooks": {
    "PostToolUse": [{
      "matcher": "Write|Edit",
      "hooks": [{
        "type": "command",
        "command": "jq -r '.tool_input.file_path // .tool_response.filePath' | grep -E '\\.(ts|js)$' && npm test || true"
      }]
    }]
  }
}
```


## Constructing a Hook (with verification)

Given an event, matcher, target file, and desired behavior, follow this flow. Each step catches a different failure class — a hook that silently does nothing is worse than no hook.

1. **Dedup check.** Read the target file. If a hook already exists on the same event+matcher, show the existing command and ask: keep it, replace it, or add alongside.

2. **Construct the command for THIS project — don't assume.** The hook receives JSON on stdin. Build a command that:
   - Extracts any needed payload safely — use `jq -r` into a quoted variable or `{ read -r f; ... "$f"; }`, NOT unquoted `| xargs` (splits on spaces)
   - Invokes the underlying tool the way this project runs it (npx/bunx/yarn/pnpm? Makefile target? globally-installed?)
   - Skips inputs the tool doesn't handle (formatters often have `--ignore-unknown`; if not, guard by extension)
   - Stays RAW for now — no `|| true`, no stderr suppression. You'll wrap it after the pipe-test passes.

3. **Pipe-test the raw command.** Synthesize the stdin payload the hook will receive and pipe it directly:
   - `Pre|PostToolUse` on `Write|Edit`: `echo '{"tool_name":"Edit","tool_input":{"file_path":"<a real file from this repo>"}}' | <cmd>`
   - `Pre|PostToolUse` on `Bash`: `echo '{"tool_name":"Bash","tool_input":{"command":"ls"}}' | <cmd>`
   - `Stop`/`UserPromptSubmit`/`SessionStart`: most commands don't read stdin, so `echo '{}' | <cmd>` suffices

   Check exit code AND side effect (file actually formatted, test actually ran). If it fails you get a real error — fix (wrong package manager? tool not installed? jq path wrong?) and retest. Once it works, wrap with `2>/dev/null || true` (unless the user wants a blocking check).

4. **Write the JSON.** Merge into the target file (schema shape in the "Hook Structure" section above). If this creates `.claude/settings.local.json` for the first time, add it to .gitignore — the Write tool doesn't auto-gitignore it.

5. **Validate syntax + schema in one shot:**

   `jq -e '.hooks.<event>[] | select(.matcher == "<matcher>") | .hooks[] | select(.type == "command") | .command' <target-file>`

   Exit 0 + prints your command = correct. Exit 4 = matcher doesn't match. Exit 5 = malformed JSON or wrong nesting. A broken settings.json silently disables ALL settings from that file — fix any pre-existing malformation too.

6. **Prove the hook fires** — only for `Pre|PostToolUse` on a matcher you can trigger in-turn (`Write|Edit` via Edit, `Bash` via Bash). `Stop`/`UserPromptSubmit`/`SessionStart` fire outside this turn — skip to step 7.

   For a **formatter** on `PostToolUse`/`Write|Edit`: introduce a detectable violation via Edit (two consecutive blank lines, bad indentation, missing semicolon — something this formatter corrects; NOT trailing whitespace, Edit strips that before writing), re-read, confirm the hook **fixed** it. For **anything else**: temporarily prefix the command in settings.json with `echo "$(date) hook fired" >> /tmp/claude-hook-check.txt; `, trigger the matching tool (Edit for `Write|Edit`, a harmless `true` for `Bash`), read the sentinel file.

   **Always clean up** — revert the violation, strip the sentinel prefix — whether the proof passed or failed.

   **If proof fails but pipe-test passed and `jq -e` passed**: the settings watcher isn't watching `.claude/` — it only watches directories that had a settings file when this session started. The hook is written correctly. Tell the user to open `/hooks` once (reloads config) or restart — you can't do this yourself; `/hooks` is a user UI menu and opening it ends this turn.

7. **Handoff.** Tell the user the hook is live (or needs `/hooks`/restart per the watcher caveat). Point them at `/hooks` to review, edit, or disable it later. The UI only shows "Ran N hooks" if a hook errors or is slow — silent success is invisible by design.


## Example Workflows

### Adding a Hook

User: "Format my code after Claude writes it"

1. **Clarify**: Which formatter? (prettier, gofmt, etc.)
2. **Read**: `.claude/settings.json` (or create if missing)
3. **Merge**: Add to existing hooks, don't replace
4. **Result**:
```json
{
  "hooks": {
    "PostToolUse": [{
      "matcher": "Write|Edit",
      "hooks": [{
        "type": "command",
        "command": "jq -r '.tool_response.filePath // .tool_input.file_path' | { read -r f; prettier --write \"$f\"; } 2>/dev/null || true"
      }]
    }]
  }
}
```

### Adding Permissions

User: "Allow npm commands without prompting"

1. **Read**: Existing permissions
2. **Merge**: Add `Bash(npm:*)` to allow array
3. **Result**: Combined with existing allows

### Environment Variables

User: "Set DEBUG=true"

1. **Decide**: User settings (global) or project settings?
2. **Read**: Target file
3. **Merge**: Add to env object
```json
{ "env": { "DEBUG": "true" } }
```

## Common Mistakes to Avoid

1. **Replacing instead of merging** - Always preserve existing settings
2. **Wrong file** - Ask user if scope is unclear
3. **Invalid JSON** - Validate syntax after changes
4. **Forgetting to read first** - Always read before write

## Troubleshooting Hooks

If a hook isn't running:
1. **Check the settings file** - Read ~/.claude/settings.json or .claude/settings.json
2. **Verify JSON syntax** - Invalid JSON silently fails
3. **Check the matcher** - Does it match the tool name? (e.g., "Bash", "Write", "Edit")
4. **Check hook type** - Is it "command", "prompt", or "agent"?
5. **Test the command** - Run the hook command manually to see if it works
6. **Use --debug** - Run `claude --debug` to see hook execution logs

## User Request

Add two hooks to .claude/settings.json (keeping the existing SessionStart hook):

1. PreToolUse hook on "Bash" matcher: blocks destructive git commands (git checkout, git clean, git reset --hard, git push --force, git branch -D). Command should check CLAUDE_TOOL_INPUT for these patterns and exit 2 with a message if found.

2. SessionStart hook (add alongside existing session-state.js hook): auto-stashes uncommitted work. Command should check if there are uncommitted changes via git status --porcelain, and if so, run git stash push -m "auto-stash-before-claude-session-$(date +%Y%m%d-%H%M%S)"

## Skill recommendations

Based on the repo research, here are the skills worth building, ranked by how much repeated instruction they eliminate:

### Tier 1 — Build these first (highest ROI)

**1. `/veracity-check`** — Phase 7 veracity pass per page
- Your active priority right now (S01-S12). You'll run this 12+ times in the near term.
- Encodes: load veracity framework + source library, run 6-phase check, place `{/* REVIEW: */}` markers, set `veracityStatus` in frontmatter, output citation report
- Prevents: re-explaining the veracity-pass.md workflow every session

**2. `/gate-check`** — Pre-phase validation
- Reads tab-status.md + decision-registry.md + blocking-items.md, confirms all prerequisites are met for a proposed phase on a given tab
- Prevents: false starts where Claude proposes blocked work, and the recurring "is IA locked yet?" back-and-forth

**3. `/content-review`** — Content-pass REVIEW mode for a single page
- Encodes: read the page, apply content-pass.md scorecard + voice-rules.md + Frameworks.mdx taxonomy, output the fixed MDX (not a to-do list), flag anything needing human decision
- Prevents: the rubber-stamping problem and the "output a to-do list when asked for a fixed page" failure mode

### Tier 2 — Build when Tier 1 is validated

**4. `/batch-audit`** — Parallel agent audit launcher
- Your best workflow pattern. Skill defines: scope (directory), checks to run, output format, acceptance criteria. Spawns agents with narrow scope, synthesises results.
- Prevents: re-specifying audit parameters each session

**5. `/terminology-scan`** — Per-tab terminology validator
- Scans all pages in a tab against locked glossary, flags undefined terms, deprecated terms, jargon used without definition at first use
- Prevents: manual terminology checking across 70+ pages per tab

**6. `/recon-execute`** — Reconsolidation executor (Phase 4.5)
- Reads approved audit dispositions, builds docs.json patch, validates no silent removals, maps upstream/downstream, executes moves with human checkpoint
- Prevents: the destructive file-move incidents and broken navigation

Want me to build any of these?

## The actual problem

The insights show 5 types of sessions you run. Each one breaks in a different way. The fix isn't more pipeline automation — it's giving Claude a **mode of working** that matches each session type, so it knows what it's allowed to do, when to stop, and what "done" looks like.

Here are the 5 co-work skills I'd recommend, mapped to your frustration patterns:

---

### 1. `/findings` — Read-only investigation mode

**When you'd use it:** "Look at X and tell me what you find." Content scans, gap analysis, repo audits, pre-decision research.

**What it enforces:**
- Read, Grep, Glob only. No Edit, no Write, no Bash that modifies anything.
- Output is a structured findings report (numbered, categorised, severity-tagged)
- Claude presents findings and stops. No "and here's how I'd fix it" — no fix proposals unless asked.
- No agents spawned without explicit approval.

**Frustration it solves:** Claude fixing as it finds (119 wrong-approach instances). The "findings before fixes" rule you keep re-stating.

---

### 2. `/checkpoint` — Step-by-step supervised execution

**When you'd use it:** "Execute this approved plan." File moves, batch edits, reconsolidation, any multi-step write operation.

**What it enforces:**
- Claude states the exact action it will take (file, change, reason) before each step
- Waits for "go" / "ok" / "proceed" before executing each step
- After each step: shows what changed, confirms success, states next step
- If anything unexpected happens, stops and reports — doesn't try to fix
- Maximum 3 files per checkpoint batch (limits blast radius)

**Frustration it solves:** Jumping ahead without permission (49 misunderstood-request signals). The "describing the next task is not approval" rule.

---

### 3. `/decide` — Decision support mode

**When you'd use it:** "I need to make a call on [blocking item]." VRAM values, tab assignments, terminology locks, any of the 8 blocking decisions.

**What it enforces:**
- Claude gathers all relevant evidence (reads source files, existing decisions, related pages)
- Presents a structured brief: context, options (max 3), trade-offs for each, recommendation with reasoning
- Does NOT make the decision — presents evidence and waits
- Once you decide, Claude writes it to decision-registry.md and updates blocking-items.md
- Confirms downstream phases unblocked by this decision

**Frustration it solves:** Open-ended questions instead of concrete proposals. Decisions made in chat that never reach the registry.

---

### 4. `/dispatch` — Parallel agent coordinator

**When you'd use it:** "Audit these 10 directories." / "Run quality checks across section X." Your highest-satisfaction pattern.

**What it enforces:**
- Claude proposes the agent batch: how many agents, what each reads, what each outputs, acceptance criteria
- Waits for approval before spawning
- All agents launch in a single message (never sequential unless dependent)
- Each agent has restricted scope (read-only unless otherwise stated)
- Claude synthesises all agent results into a single rollup report
- Agents self-validate before reporting (no unchecked claims)

**Frustration it solves:** Needing to re-specify audit parameters every session. Agents that don't self-test.

---

### 5. `/co-review` — Collaborative page review

**When you'd use it:** "Let's review this page together." Content-pass reviews, veracity checks, editorial passes.

**What it enforces:**
- Claude reads the page critically (not rubber-stamps)
- Presents issues as a numbered list with line references, severity, and proposed fix for each
- You approve/reject/modify each fix individually
- Claude applies only approved fixes, one at a time, using targeted edits (never full file rewrites)
- After all fixes applied, Claude re-reads and confirms the page passes
- Flags anything needing human verification separately from fixable issues

**Frustration it solves:** Rubber-stamping. Full file overwrites. Applying all fixes without approval. The "output a to-do list when asked for a fixed page" failure mode (this one outputs both — the list for your review, then the fixes on approval).

---

### How they compose

A typical session might flow:

1. `/findings` on a section → you get the report
2. `/decide` on a blocking item surfaced by findings → decision recorded
3. `/checkpoint` to execute the approved fixes → step by step
4. `/co-review` on the finished pages → editorial pass

Or for batch work:

1. `/dispatch` to audit 10 directories → rollup report
2. `/decide` on issues that need human calls → decisions recorded
3. `/checkpoint` to execute the remediation plan → gated execution

---

Want me to build these? If so, which ones first — or all 5?

## ASSISTANT
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

You're right. I was solving for content tasks, not for how Claude works with you. Let me reframe.

The actual problems:

1. **Claude loses the thread** — drifts from the outcome mid-session
2. **No structured phase progression** — research → audit → co-design → architecture → test → iterate
3. **Main thread blocks** — Claude does heavy work inline instead of delegating to agents

Here's what I'd build:

---

### `/thread` — Session anchor

Sets the outcome at session start. Claude writes it down (plan or task tracker), restates it before each phase transition, and every proposed action must trace back to it. If Claude proposes something that doesn't connect to the outcome, it's drift — flag it and pull back.

This is the fix for "Claude forgets what we're doing."

---

### `/research` — Agent-delegated investigation

You state what you need to know. Claude proposes agent scopes (what each reads, what each returns), you approve, agents run in background. Main thread stays free — you can talk, think, redirect. When agents return, Claude synthesises into a single brief. No fixes, no proposals — just structured findings.

---

### `/design` — First-principles co-creation

No reading files. No executing. Pure thinking mode. Claude proposes a design based on research findings, you shape it together. Output is an architecture doc (structure, decisions, trade-offs, test criteria). Claude challenges its own assumptions — no rubber-stamping its own ideas. You push back, Claude iterates the design, not the code.

---

### `/build` — Execute approved architecture

Takes the architecture doc from `/design` as input. Claude breaks it into agent-scoped tasks, proposes the batch, you approve. Agents execute in background. Main thread tracks progress. Each agent validates its own output against the test criteria from the design doc before reporting done.

---

### `/iterate` — Review and loop

Reviews build output against test criteria. Identifies gaps. Proposes which phase to loop back to (more research? redesign? rebuild specific piece?). You decide. Prevents the "fix everything now" instinct — routes back to the right phase.

---

### How they chain

```
/thread  →  define outcome
/research  →  agents gather, main thread free
/design  →  think together, no execution
/build  →  agents execute, checkpointed
/iterate  →  review, loop to right phase
```

Each one keeps the main thread responsive. Heavy work goes to agents. The thread anchor persists across all phases.

Want me to build these?

## ASSISTANT

Good that the hooks are working.

On "not recommending best approaches" — that's the core issue the research confirms. Your governance framework prevents Claude from doing wrong things, but it's pushed Claude into mechanical compliance. The rule says "recommend and suggest what you think to be true" but in practice Claude defaults to "what do you want me to do?" because every other rule is about not overstepping.

The co-work skills need to encode **quality of thinking**, not just process discipline. Here's what I mean:

### What "recommend best approaches" looks like in each phase

**Research** — Claude doesn't just read and list what it found. It synthesises, identifies patterns, brings external knowledge (content strategy, IA best practices, docs architecture principles), and says "based on what I found, here's what I think the best approach is and why."

**Design** — Claude doesn't wait for you to design and then validate. It brings a first-principles proposal: "here's how this should work based on [principle], here's where your current approach deviates, here's what I'd change." It challenges, not rubber-stamps.

**Build** — Claude doesn't just execute the spec. It flags when an implementation creates tech debt, when there's a better pattern, when the architecture doesn't hold up under the actual content.

**Project management** — Claude doesn't just track state. It proactively identifies bottlenecks ("these 8 blocking decisions have been open for 2 days and are blocking 5 tabs"), recommends priority changes, and surfaces risks before they bite.

### The tension in your current system

Your ai-rules-guides.md says: *"Always suggest and recommend what you think to be true for confirmation — don't just ask stupid questions and apply learned helplessness."*

But the 13 agent rules, 7 failure mode docs, and mandatory canonical-quote-before-action pattern trained Claude into exactly that learned helplessness. The rules say "think for yourself" but every enforcement mechanism punishes initiative.

The skills need to resolve this by being explicit: **bring your expertise first, then wait for approval on the action, not the thinking.** Claude should think freely and recommend confidently — the gate is on execution, not on having an opinion.

### What I'd build

| Skill | What it encodes | What changes |
|---|---|---|
| `/pm` | Proactive project management — track state, surface bottlenecks, recommend priorities, identify when blocked decisions are costing time | Claude stops being a passive state reporter and starts being a project partner |
| `/research` | Synthesise + recommend, not just list findings. Bring external best practices. "Here's what I found AND here's what I think it means" | Claude stops producing flat inventories and starts producing actionable analysis |
| `/design` | First-principles co-creation. Claude proposes architecture based on best practice, challenges deviations, defends recommendations. Output = architecture doc with rationale | Claude stops waiting for your design and starts co-designing |
| `/build` | Execute with quality judgment. Flag tech debt as it forms. Self-test against design criteria. Raise concerns before they become problems | Claude stops being a blind executor |
| `/iterate` | Critical review against best practice, not just against the spec. "This works per spec but here's a better pattern" | Claude stops rubber-stamping its own output |
| `/thread` | Session anchor + outcome tracking. Prevents drift. But also: Claude actively relates each step back to the outcome and flags when work is diverging | Claude stops losing the plot mid-session |

### Next step

I can build these now. But given your point about jumping to execution before architecture — should I first draft the skill architecture (what each skill contains, how they interact, what "best practice recommendation" looks like concretely) for us to co-design before I write any SKILL.md files?

## ASSISTANT
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Good. Architecture first, then build, then iterate against your actual threads. Here's the design.

---

## Skill Architecture: Co-Work Process Skills

### Shared principles (apply to ALL skills)

1. **Think freely, gate on execution.** Claude recommends, challenges, proposes with reasoning. The approval gate is on doing things, not on having opinions.
2. **Main thread = thinking space.** Heavy work (file reads, audits, bulk operations) goes to background agents. Main thread is for human-Claude dialogue.
3. **Thread anchor is always live.** Every action traces to the session outcome. If it doesn't connect, flag the drift.
4. **Recommend with reasoning.** Never "what would you like?" Always "here's what I'd do and why — does that work?"
5. **Challenge deviations.** If the current approach contradicts best practice, say so with the principle and the reasoning. Don't silently comply.

---

### `/thread` — Session anchor

**Trigger:** Start of any working session, or when drift is detected.

**What Claude does:**
- Asks: "What's the outcome for this session?" (one sentence)
- Writes it to the task tracker
- Before each phase transition or new action: restates outcome, confirms current action connects
- If proposed work doesn't connect to outcome: "This doesn't trace back to [outcome] — is this a scope change or should we refocus?"

**Output:** Outcome statement, visible in task tracker throughout session.

**Not allowed to:** Let the outcome go stale. If 3+ actions have passed without referencing it, restate.

**Hands off to:** Any other skill. Thread stays active underneath all of them.

---

### `/research` — Investigate and recommend

**Trigger:** "I need to understand X before we decide/build."

**What Claude does:**
1. Proposes research scope: what to read, what agents to spawn, what questions to answer
2. On approval, spawns agents in background — main thread stays free
3. When agents return, synthesises into a brief:
   - **What I found** — structured findings, not a flat list
   - **What I think it means** — patterns, gaps, risks, connections
   - **What I'd recommend** — best approach with reasoning, referencing external best practice where relevant (IA principles, content strategy, docs architecture)
   - **What needs your decision** — items where the research doesn't resolve the question

**Output:** Research brief with findings + analysis + recommendation + decision items.

**Not allowed to:** Present findings without analysis. If Claude doesn't have an opinion on what the findings mean, it's not done.

**Hands off to:** `/design` (if building something new) or `/decide` moment within the thread (if a blocking decision surfaced).

---

### `/design` — First-principles co-creation

**Trigger:** "We need to figure out how X should work."

**What Claude does:**
1. States the design problem in one sentence
2. Proposes an architecture based on first principles — not based on "what exists now" unless existing work is sound
3. Walks through:
   - **Principles** — what rules govern this design (e.g., "every page answers one sub-question of the arriving question")
   - **Structure** — how the pieces fit together
   - **Trade-offs** — what this design sacrifices and why that's acceptable
   - **Test criteria** — how we'll know if this works (concrete, verifiable)
4. Challenges its own proposal: "The weakness here is..."
5. You shape it — push back, redirect, override. Claude iterates the design in conversation.
6. Once agreed, Claude writes the architecture doc to a file

**Output:** Architecture doc with: problem statement, principles, structure, trade-offs, test criteria.

**Not allowed to:** Skip to implementation details. No file paths, no code, no "here's how I'd build it" — pure design thinking. Implementation comes in `/build`.

**Hands off to:** `/build` (to execute the design).

---

### `/build` — Execute approved architecture

**Trigger:** "Go build it." Only after a `/design` output exists or an approved plan.

**What Claude does:**
1. Reads the architecture doc / approved plan
2. Breaks work into agent-scoped tasks — proposes the batch with scope, inputs, outputs, and acceptance criteria per agent
3. On approval, launches agents in background
4. As agents return: validates output against the design's test criteria
5. Flags anything that deviates: "This agent's output doesn't meet criterion X — here's what's wrong and what I'd do"
6. Reports completion with: what's done, what passed, what needs attention

**Output:** Built artefacts + test results against design criteria.

**Not allowed to:** Build without an approved design. If no architecture doc exists, redirect to `/design` first. Also not allowed to silently accept agent output that fails test criteria.

**Hands off to:** `/iterate` (to review and refine).

---

### `/iterate` — Review, test, refine

**Trigger:** After `/build` completes, or when reviewing any existing work.

**What Claude does:**
1. Reviews output against:
   - The design's test criteria (does it do what we designed?)
   - Best practice (is the design itself still right, or did building reveal a flaw?)
   - Thread outcome (does the result actually serve the session goal?)
2. Categorises findings:
   - **Pass** — meets criteria, no action
   - **Fix** — doesn't meet criteria, fix is clear, propose it
   - **Redesign** — the design itself needs to change (routes back to `/design`)
   - **Research** — we discovered something we don't understand (routes back to `/research`)
3. Proposes next action: which phase to loop to, or "done — this meets the outcome"

**Output:** Review report with pass/fix/redesign/research categorisation + recommended next phase.

**Not allowed to:** Rubber-stamp. If everything passes, Claude must state specifically what it checked and why it's confident. "Looks good" is not a review.

**Hands off to:** `/design` (if redesign needed), `/research` (if gaps found), `/build` (if fixes approved), or done.

---

### `/pm` — Proactive project management

**Trigger:** Any session, especially when working across multiple threads or plans.

**What Claude does:**
1. Reads project-state.md, tab-status.md, decision-registry.md, blocking-items.md
2. Reports state — but not just a flat status dump. Structured as:
   - **What's moving** — active work, recent completions
   - **What's stuck** — blocked items, how long they've been blocked, what they're costing
   - **What I'd prioritise** — based on dependency graph, what unblocks the most downstream work
   - **Risks** — things that will become problems if not addressed soon
3. Proactively surfaces: "These 3 decisions have been open for N days and are blocking M items. Here's what I'd recommend for each."
4. After any work completes: updates project-state.md, states what's unblocked

**Output:** Proactive status with recommendations, not passive state report.

**Not allowed to:** Just list state without analysis. Must always include "what I'd prioritise and why."

**Hands off to:** Whatever phase the priority recommendation points to.

---

### How they compose

```
/thread  →  anchor the session
    ↓
/pm  →  "here's where things stand, here's what I'd work on"
    ↓
/research  →  agents investigate, main thread free
    ↓
/design  →  co-create the architecture together
    ↓
/build  →  agents execute, validate against design
    ↓
/iterate  →  review, categorise, loop or done
    ↑__________|  (back to research/design/build as needed)
```

`/pm` can be invoked at any point. `/thread` persists underneath everything.

---

### Testing plan

After building each skill, we test it on a real thread:

1. **`/thread` + `/pm`** — test on your current orchestrators thread. Does it anchor correctly? Does `/pm` surface the right priorities?
2. **`/research`** — test on one of the blocking decisions (e.g., VRAM values or glossary scope). Does it synthesise and recommend, or just list?
3. **`/design`** — test on a real design problem (e.g., the co-work skills themselves, or a tab IA). Does Claude propose and challenge, or wait?
4. **`/build` + `/iterate`** — test on a small scoped build. Does it validate against criteria? Does iterate catch real issues?

Each test: use it, note what's wrong, refine the skill, test again. We iterate the skills using the iterate skill.

---

Ready to build? I'd start with `/thread` and `/pm` since those apply to every session and we can test them immediately.

---

Now — the hooks issue. You're saying the auto-stash SessionStart hook is reverting unsaved/unstaged files. That's because `git stash push` stashes uncommitted changes and then **reverts the working directory to clean state**. So at session start, your in-progress edits disappear from the working tree (they're safe in the stash, but your editor shows the old version).

The fix: the hook should stash but NOT clean the working tree — or better, it should just **commit a WIP checkpoint** instead of stashing. Let me check what's in settings.json now and fix it.


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
## ASSISTANT
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[TOOL: Read]
{
  "file_path": "/Users/alisonhaire/Documents/Livepeer/Docs-v2-dev/.claude/settings.json"
}


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
## ASSISTANT
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

I see the problem. `git stash push` removes changes from the working tree — so your editor shows reverted files. Two options:

**Option A: Keep stash but immediately pop it back.** Stash creates the safety snapshot, pop restores your working state. The stash entry persists in the reflog even after pop. Net effect: safety backup exists, working tree untouched.

**Option B: Remove the auto-stash hook entirely.** The destructive-git-blocker (PreToolUse) already prevents the worst scenarios. The stash was belt-and-suspenders — maybe the belt is enough.

I'd recommend **Option A** — it gives you the safety net without disrupting your working tree. The stash snapshot is recoverable via `git stash list` / `git reflog` even after pop.

Which do you want, or do you want to drop the hook altogether?

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
## ASSISTANT
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Here's the gap. The `cross-agent-packager` is about syncing skills across different AI tools (Codex, Cursor, etc.) — it doesn't govern what spawned sub-agents receive as instructions.

Right now when `/research` or `/build` spawn agents, the instruction is whatever Claude writes ad-hoc in the prompt parameter. No standard brief, no quality contract, no thread connection.

What's needed: an `/agent-brief` skill that defines the **standard instruction template** every spawned agent receives. It would encode:

1. **Thread context** — one sentence: what the session outcome is, how this agent's task serves it
2. **Scope** — what to read, what to produce, what NOT to touch
3. **Quality contract** — self-validate before returning, no unchecked claims, recommend don't just list
4. **Return format** — structured output the main thread can synthesise
5. **Failure protocol** — if a dependency is missing or the task can't be completed, return immediately with what's wrong instead of producing partial garbage

This is the bridge between the main-thread skills (`/research`, `/build`) and the agents they spawn. Without it, the skills govern how Claude proposes the agent batch, but the agents themselves are ungoverned.

Want me to build it?

can threads get context from other threads? what else was in /insights report as pain points? do we need to update claude.md? where are the gaps and issues still ?


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
## ASSISTANT
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Good questions — let me hit all four.

### 1. Can threads get context from other threads?

Not natively. Each Claude Code session starts fresh. Cross-session context comes from:

| Mechanism | What it does | You have it? |
|---|---|---|
| CLAUDE.md | Read every session. Rules, state, standards | Yes |
| Auto-memory | Persistent memory files Claude reads/writes | Yes |
| claude-mem plugin | Automatic context capture + injection across sessions | Just installed |
| Project state files | Manually maintained, read at session start | Yes (project-state.md) |
| `--continue` / `--resume` | Resume a specific prior session with full context | Available |
| Session log in CLAUDE.md | Append-only record of what happened each session | Yes |

**The gap:** Your skills don't have a mechanism for thread A to pass findings to thread B except through files. If `/research` produces a brief in one session, the next session only knows about it if:
- It's saved to a file at a known path
- CLAUDE.md or project-state.md points to it
- claude-mem captures it automatically

This is mostly solved by your existing file-based system — but the skills should explicitly write outputs to files, not just return them in chat. `/research` and `/build` do this. `/design` does this (writes architecture doc). `/pm` updates project-state.md.

### 2. What else was in the insights report?

Revisiting the pain points — here's what's addressed vs still open:

| Pain point | Addressed? | By what |
|---|---|---|
| Destructive git commands | Yes | PreToolUse hook |
| Uncommitted work vulnerability (7 commits / 52 sessions) | Partial | Auto-stash hook creates reflog snapshot, but commit rate is still low |
| Jumping ahead without permission | Yes | `/thread`, `/design` before `/build` |
| Asking instead of investigating | Yes | Skills encode "read before asking, recommend don't ask" |
| Rubber-stamping reviews | Yes | `/iterate` anti-patterns section |
| Forgetting thread outcome | Yes | `/thread` drift detection |
| No best-practice recommendations | Yes | All skills encode "recommend with reasoning" |
| **Leaked private data in public GitHub issue** | **No** | No guardrail exists |
| **59 failed fix attempts on VSCode extensions** | **No** | No "stop after N failures" circuit breaker |
| **Long correction cycles from vague first messages** | **Partial** | Skills help but nothing enforces structured first message |
| **Agent quality — unchecked claims** | **Yes** | `/agent-brief` quality contract |
| **Main thread blocked by heavy work** | **Yes** | All skills delegate to background agents |

**Still unaddressed:**
1. **Sensitive data leak prevention** — no hook or skill prevents Claude from posting private info to public services
2. **Circuit breaker** — no mechanism to stop Claude after N failed attempts at the same thing
3. **First-message structure** — nothing enforces the user providing enough context upfront (though `/thread` helps by forcing outcome definition)

### 3. Do we need to update CLAUDE.md?

**Yes.** Two gaps:

**Gap A: CLAUDE.md doesn't reference the co-work skills.** It's read every session. If it doesn't tell Claude these skills exist and when to use them, they'll be ignored. The "Co-creation rules" section needs to reference the skill workflow.

**Gap B: Skill discoverability.** Your skills live at `ai-tools/ai-skills/*/SKILL.md`. Claude Code auto-discovers skills from `.claude/skills/*/SKILL.md`. Your existing skills work because CLAUDE.md tells Claude about them explicitly — but the new co-work skills aren't mentioned yet.

### 4. Where are the remaining gaps?

| Gap | Impact | Fix |
|---|---|---|
| CLAUDE.md doesn't reference co-work skills | Skills won't be used in new sessions | Add skill workflow section to CLAUDE.md |
| No sensitive data guardrail | Risk of leaking private info to public services | PreToolUse hook on GitHub MCP tools / Bash commands that post publicly |
| No circuit breaker | Claude can spiral on a failing approach indefinitely | Could be a hook or a `/iterate` rule (2 failures = escalate is there, but not enforced mechanically) |
| Skills not tested on real threads | Don't know if they actually work | Next step — test on orchestrators thread |
| Auto-stash doesn't solve low commit rate | Work is still vulnerable between sessions | This is a habit change, not a tooling fix |
| No `/dispatch` skill | Was in original proposal, handles parallel audit batches | Could be a thin wrapper around `/research` + `/agent-brief` |

**My recommendation:** Update CLAUDE.md to reference the skills (highest impact, 5 minutes), then test on a real thread. The sensitive data hook and circuit breaker are worth building but lower urgency.

Want me to update CLAUDE.md with the skill workflow section?

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
## ASSISTANT
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Tasks saved. Now addressing each point:

---

### Named file conventions for skill outputs

Good idea. Each skill should write to a predictable path so any thread can find prior work. I'd propose:

```
workspace/thread-outputs/
  research/
    {topic}-brief.md          # e.g. glossary-scope-brief.md
  design/
    {name}-architecture.md    # e.g. veracity-pass-architecture.md
  build/
    {name}-build-report.md
  iterate/
    {name}-review-report.md
  pm/
    project-state.md          # already exists at its current path
```

This gives every skill output a home. Any thread can find prior research by checking `workspace/thread-outputs/research/`. I'll update the skills with this.

---

### Vague message handling

Yes — this fits naturally in `/thread`. At Step 1 (define outcome), if the message is vague, Claude should propose what it thinks the user means and refine:

```
"I think you're asking for [X]. Specifically:
- [concrete interpretation 1]
- [concrete interpretation 2]
Is that right, or should I adjust?"
```

Not "what do you want?" — always "here's what I think you mean."

---

### Looping / circuit breaker

The loop problem isn't just "stop after N failures" — it's Claude not doing root-cause analysis. The fix is a **debugging discipline** baked into the skills:

> After 2 failed attempts at the same approach:
> 1. STOP executing
> 2. State what you tried and why it failed (both times)
> 3. List the facts: error messages, file state, what changed between attempts
> 4. Propose a different approach based on root-cause analysis
> 5. Wait for approval before trying again

This goes in every skill's anti-patterns section plus `/iterate`.

---

### Repo file mess

Two parts to this:

**A. File placement discipline** — baked into `/build` and `/agent-brief`: agents must propose a file path with reasoning before writing. If the path is root or doesn't group by concern, the skill flags it:

> "This file would land in root. Recommended location: `workspace/[concern]/[file]` because [reasoning]. Confirm or redirect."

**B. Stale file cleanup** — this is a periodic hygiene task. I'd add a step to `/pm` that scans for:
- Files in root that should be grouped
- Files older than N days with no references from other files
- Orphan outputs from completed threads

`/pm` surfaces these as "repo hygiene" items in its risk section.

---

### Worktrees vs branches

Your frustration with worktrees is valid — they accumulate. Options:

**Option A: Branch-based isolation with cleanup hook.** Claude works on a named branch (e.g. `claude/veracity-pass`). A SessionEnd hook lists any branches Claude created. You merge or delete explicitly. No worktree sprawl.

**Option B: Worktrees with mandatory cleanup.** A Stop hook runs `git worktree list` and flags any worktrees created this session that weren't merged. Forces explicit decision: merge, keep, or delete.

**Option C: Stay on main branch, use stash checkpoints.** Current approach. Simpler, but no isolation for experimental work.

I'd recommend **Option A** — branches give isolation without the filesystem sprawl of worktrees. The branch exists in git, not as a separate directory. Cleanup is `git branch -d`, not finding and removing directory trees.

---

### CLAUDE.md constraining thinking

Yes, this is a real tension. Your CLAUDE.md is ~400 lines of rules. Every rule exists because of a real failure, but collectively they push Claude toward mechanical compliance. The "validate every action with a canonical quote" rule (Rule 2.13) is the most constraining — it literally requires Claude to cite authority before thinking.

My recommendation: when we update CLAUDE.md with skill references, **replace some of the defensive rules with the skills themselves**. Instead of 13 granular agent rules, point to `/agent-brief`. Instead of listing all the "never do" items, the skills encode what TO do. Fewer rules, more positive patterns.

The principle: **CLAUDE.md sets the tone and points to skills. Skills encode the detail.** CLAUDE.md should be shorter after this, not longer.

---

Now let me build: update the skills with named file conventions, add vague-message handling to `/thread`, add the debugging/anti-loop discipline, add file placement to `/build` + `/agent-brief`, add repo hygiene to `/pm`, and build `/dispatch`.

## ASSISTANT

All updates applied. Here's what changed:

**Skills updated:**
- `/thread` — added vague-message handling (propose interpretation, don't ask open questions) + anti-loop discipline (2 failures = stop, root-cause analyse, propose different approach)
- `/build` — added file placement discipline (never root, group by concern, named output paths)
- `/pm` — added repo hygiene scan (root files, orphan outputs, stale artefacts)
- `/agent-brief` — added file output convention + anti-loop in failure protocol
- `/iterate` — strengthened the loop-prevention anti-pattern with specific steps

**Skills built:**
- `/dispatch` — [ai-tools/ai-skills/dispatch/SKILL.md](ai-tools/ai-skills/dispatch/SKILL.md)

---

Now — your worktree question. My recommendation:

**Branches with cleanup, not worktrees.** Specifically:
- Experimental or multi-session work goes on a named branch (`claude/{topic}`)
- When complete, merge to main working branch and delete the branch
- A `/pm` hygiene check can list stale branches (older than 7 days, unmerged) the same way it lists stale files

This avoids the worktree sprawl problem. Branches are lightweight (just a git pointer), don't create filesystem copies, and are cleaned up with `git branch -d`. The PreToolUse hook already blocks `git checkout` from Claude — so branch creation and switching would need explicit approval, which is the right gate.

Want me to add branch management to `/pm` and `/build`?

---

### On CLAUDE.md constraining thinking

Yes, I think it does. The current CLAUDE.md is ~400 lines of "don't do X." The skills encode the positive patterns. My recommendation for the CLAUDE.md update (queued task):

- **Slim the rules section** — replace the 13 agent rules with "follow `/agent-brief`"
- **Replace "never do" lists** with skill references — "use `/thread` for session management, `/research` before `/design`, `/design` before `/build`"
- **Keep the tone-setting section** — project identity, co-creation philosophy, voice rules
- **Move operational detail into skills** — CLAUDE.md points, skills detail

Net effect: shorter CLAUDE.md that says "think freely, here are the skills that encode how we work" instead of 400 lines of defensive rules.

Option A: Branch-based isolation with cleanup hook. Claude works on a named branch (e.g. claude/veracity-pass). A SessionEnd hook lists any branches Claude created. You merge or delete explicitly. No worktree sprawl.

Option B: Worktrees with mandatory cleanup. A Stop hook runs git worktree list and flags any worktrees created this session that weren't merged. Forces explicit decision: merge, keep, or delete.

Option C: Stay on main branch, use stash checkpoints. Current approach. Simpler, but no isolation for experimental work.

I'd recommend Option A — branches give isolation without the filesystem sprawl of worktrees. The branch exists in git, not as a separate directory. Cleanup is git branch -d, not finding and removing directory trees.

CLAUDE.md constraining thinking
Yes, this is a real tension. Your CLAUDE.md is ~400 lines of rules. Every rule exists because of a real failure, but collectively they push Claude toward mechanical compliance. The "validate every action with a canonical quote" rule (Rule 2.13) is the most constraining — it literally requires Claude to cite authority before thinking.

My recommendation: when we update CLAUDE.md with skill references, replace some of the defensive rules with the skills themselves. Instead of 13 granular agent rules, point to /agent-brief. Instead of listing all the "never do" items, the skills encode what TO do. Fewer rules, more positive patterns.

The principle: CLAUDE.md sets the tone and points to skills. Skills encode the detail. CLAUDE.md should be shorter after this, not longer.

Now let me build: update the skills with named file conventions, add vague-message handling to /thread, add the debugging/anti-loop discipline, add file placement to /build + /agent-brief, add repo hygiene to /pm, and build /dispatch.

---

Now — your question about pipeline skills. You're right to be wary. The co-work skills are generic process patterns. Pipeline skills would encode domain-specific knowledge about veracity passes, content reviews, etc. — and that knowledge is still being refined through the actual work.

**How to flag them as knowledge-limited and under test:**

Add `metadata.status: "draft"` to the SKILL.md frontmatter. The `metadata` map supports any string key. Then in each skill's body, add a section:

```markdown
## Status: Draft — Learning While Doing

This skill is being tested and refined during active content pipeline work.
Known limitations are logged below. Updates happen after each real-world use.

### Known limitations
- [updated as we discover them]

### Test log
| Date | Used on | What worked | What didn't | Changes made |
|---|---|---|---|---|
```

This way the skill itself is the test record. Each time you use it on real work, you log what worked and what didn't, and update the skill. The pipeline skills build up knowledge through use rather than trying to get them right upfront.

Want me to add this pattern to the existing co-work skills too, or just hold it for when we build the pipeline skills?

## ASSISTANT
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The co-work skills aren't working yet because they're files Claude reads, not enforced behaviour. This session proved that — I had `/thread` written out and still jumped ahead, still drifted, still needed babysitting.

**Two problems to solve:**

**1. Making the co-work skills stick.** The skills need to be tested on real threads and iterated until the behaviour actually changes. The `status: "draft"` + test log pattern applies here too — every time a skill fails to prevent the behaviour it's designed to prevent (like I just demonstrated), that gets logged as a known limitation and the skill gets tightened. The CLAUDE.md update helps because it's loaded into every session context, but skills only work if Claude actually reads and follows them at the right moment.

**2. Pipeline skills — building through use, not upfront.** Don't build them as separate skills now. Instead, when you start a pipeline task (e.g. veracity pass on S01), use the co-work skills (`/thread` → `/research` → `/design` → `/build` → `/iterate`) to run that pipeline task. The pipeline knowledge gets captured in the architecture docs and thread outputs naturally. After doing 2-3 pipeline tasks this way, the patterns that repeat become the pipeline skills — built from evidence, not speculation.

So the answer: don't build pipeline skills yet. Use the co-work skills to do pipeline work. The pipeline skills emerge from what actually works. The co-work skills get tested and tightened at the same time. Both improve through real use.

## ASSISTANT
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Yes, it helps a lot. It explains exactly why the skills matter and what they need to do:

- **TodoWrite + `/thread`** = your external working memory. I hold the state, you think freely.
- **Backlog capture** = when a new idea hits mid-task, I log it immediately (to TodoWrite or a backlog file) and we stay on the current task. The idea isn't lost, the thread isn't derailed.
- **Structured proposals** = I don't ask "what do you want?" — I propose what I think you mean. You refine. Lower cognitive load on the organising side, full bandwidth for thinking.
- **High standards + process fidelity** = no shortcuts, no approximations, no rubber stamps. The autism side demands precision and consistency. The skills encode that.

The gap this fills in the skills: none of them currently have a "capture to backlog" step. When you throw out an idea mid-task, I should log it and come back — not chase it or ignore it. I'll add that to `/thread` as a pattern.

What are we working on next?

Logged to backlog. The reason: Claude doesn't read the folder's existing structure or governance docs before writing files. It pattern-matches on the component name ("BadgeWrapper" → badge → elements) instead of checking what the canonical folder taxonomy actually says.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
## ASSISTANT
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The knowledge exists but is fragmented across 3 files. Here's what I'd recommend:

**The problem:** Claude pattern-matches against generic React/Next.js and suggests imports, hooks, and patterns that break in Mintlify. The constraints ARE documented (`snippetsWiki/mintlify-behaviour.mdx`, `page-authoring/SKILL.md`, `components/README.md`) but Claude doesn't read them before writing components or MDX.

**The fix — two parts:**

**1. A single Mintlify constraints reference** (like the component-placement reference we just built). Consolidates the top mistakes into one file Claude reads before writing. Quick-ref, not encyclopaedic:

| Don't | Do instead |
|---|---|
| `import { useState } from 'react'` | Just use `useState` — globally available |
| `import { Card, Tabs, Accordion }` | Just use them — Mintlify globals |
| `import Foo from '../components/Foo'` | `import Foo from '/snippets/components/.../Foo.jsx'` |
| Inline styles / hex colours | Component props or CSS variables |
| Cross-JSX imports (JSX importing JSX) | Define data in parent MDX, pass through scope |
| CSS `color` on custom icons | Theme-aware SVG files with internal CSS |
| Server-side patterns / `fs` / `path` | Client-only — no SSR |

**2. Add to `/build` and `/agent-brief`:** "Before writing any MDX or component file, read the Mintlify constraints reference."

Same pattern as the component-placement fix — a reference file Claude reads, pointed to by the skills.

Want me to build this now, or park it? The source material already exists in `mintlify-behaviour.mdx` — it's mostly consolidation.

<ide_opened_file>The user opened the file /Users/alisonhaire/Documents/Livepeer/Docs-v2-dev/v2/solutions/daydream/overview.mdx in the IDE. This may or may not be related to the current task.</ide_opened_file>
ok is there a /diagnose or investigate process or skill? 

how would I enable what we've built in a currently running session?


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
## ASSISTANT
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

No `/diagnose` or `/investigate` skill exists. `/research` covers investigation but it's scoped to "understand before deciding/building" — not "something is broken, figure out why."

A `/diagnose` skill would encode the debugging discipline that's currently missing:

1. Reproduce — confirm the problem exists and get the exact error
2. Gather facts — error messages, file state, what changed, what was expected
3. Hypothesise — rank likely causes from evidence, not guessing
4. Test one hypothesis at a time — smallest change that confirms or eliminates
5. Fix the root cause, not the symptom
6. Verify the fix didn't break anything else

This is the skill that prevents the 59-failed-attempts loop pattern. Want me to build it?

---

On enabling in a running session: you can't hot-reload skills mid-session. But you can tell Claude to read one:

```
Read ai-tools/ai-skills/thread/SKILL.md and follow it for this session.
```

Or for all of them:

```
Read all SKILL.md files in ai-tools/ai-skills/thread/, pm/, research/, design/, build/, iterate/, dispatch/, agent-brief/ and follow them.
```

New sessions pick them up automatically via CLAUDE.md's skill table. But a session that started before the skills were written needs the explicit read instruction.

## Staleness audit

| Framework | Status | Key issues |
|---|---|---|
| **Component governance** | Partially stale | Component counts aspirational not actual (118 spec vs 45 real). `badges/` sub-niche undocumented. `examples/` folders undocumented. `page-containers/` empty. |

| **Automations** | Current but blocked | Plan is thorough and execution-ready. 0% executed — blocked on SCRIPT-GOVERNANCE Task 15c. |
| **AI tools governance** | Current | 95% complete, maintenance mode. Minor stale ref (completion-report mentions removed `invoke_when` field). |
| **Repo structure governance** | Current | Locked and actively maintained. Phase 0 done, Phase 1-2 heavily executed. |
| **DOCUMENTATION** | Current | Model locked, execution blocked on human review. Most comprehensive governance work — 10 concern audits, cross-cutting synthesis. |
| **TOOLING** | Current | lpd audit complete, Layer 1 validator partially implemented. |

## Existing governance index work

- **`workspace/plan/active/index.md`** exists but is stale (2026-03-20, missing DOCUMENTATION plan, uses old `tasks/` paths)
- **DOCUMENTATION plan** has the most comprehensive cross-cutting governance work (master audit across 10 concerns)
- **`docs-guide/policies/`** already has 16 governance policy files — this is the enforcement hub
- **`docs-guide/frameworks/`** has 6 prescriptive guidance files
- **No single canonical governance index exists yet**

## Placement recommendation

**`docs-guide/policies/governance-index.mdx`** — because:
- All 16 existing governance enforcement docs live in `policies/`
- Precedent: `docs-guide-structure-policy.mdx` is self-referential governance in `policies/`
- An index is an enforcement map, not guidance — belongs with policies

## What the index should contain

1. **Governed surfaces** — what's governed, by which plan, by which policy doc
2. **Decision rules** — the key placement/classification questions per surface (component categories, script types, etc.)
3. **Staleness flags** — which frameworks need updating (component counts, script paths)
4. **Cross-plan dependencies** — what blocks what
5. **Quick-ref for Claude** — "before writing X, read Y"

The staleness issues (component counts, script paths) should be flagged in the index but NOT fixed now — those are separate remediation tasks.

can we have a hook that asks me if i want to commit? or can the chat ?


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
## ASSISTANT
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The chat can already commit — you just say "commit this" and Claude runs git commands. But for a prompt that asks you proactively, there are two options:

**Option A: Stop hook** — when Claude stops (finishes a task), it asks "Want me to commit these changes?" This fires automatically at natural breakpoints.

**Option B: PostToolUse hook on Write|Edit** — after every file change, Claude gets a reminder to offer a commit checkpoint. This would be noisy though.

I'd recommend **Option A** — a Stop hook that checks for uncommitted changes and asks. It only fires when Claude finishes, not mid-work. Want me to build it?

# Claude Code Insights

151 sessions total · 87 analyzed · 2,108 messages · 376h · 5 commits
2026-03-08 to 2026-03-26

## At a Glance

**What's working:** You've developed a sophisticated approach to Claude Code, especially your use of agent delegation for parallel audits and batch quality checks across your Livepeer docs — that architecture audit session producing 6 files via parallel agents was a standout. You've also shown real initiative building custom skills, hooks-based governance, and CLAUDE.md coordination systems to tame Claude's failure modes, essentially engineering your own guardrails. See _Impressive Things You Did_.

**What's hindering you:** On Claude's side, the pattern of acting before reading is your biggest pain point — Claude repeatedly ignores existing plans, writes to wrong branches, and makes unauthorized changes, which in one case permanently destroyed weeks of uncommitted work. On your side, long marathon sessions (sometimes 100+ minutes) let errors compound badly; by the time you're correcting Claude's fifth mistake, the session context is too degraded to recover. See _Where Things Go Wrong_.

**Quick wins to try:** Try using **hooks** to automatically enforce rules like 'commit before any multi-file operation' or 'never run git checkout without confirmation' — this removes the need to manually police Claude's most destructive tendencies. Also consider **headless mode** for your batch doc quality checks, since those are well-defined enough to run non-interactively and would free you from babysitting the process. See _Features to Try_.

**Ambitious workflows:** As models get better at self-verification, you'll be able to define acceptance criteria for doc rewrites and let Claude loop on its own output until it passes — eliminating the 'slop review' cycle that ate so many of your sessions. Your parallel agent audit pattern is also perfectly positioned to scale: imagine running 10 simultaneous agents checking links, style, nav accuracy, and component usage across your entire docs site, merging into one report in minutes instead of hours. See _On the Horizon_.

## Insights Summary: 87 sessions, 376h, 2,108 messages

### The numbers

- **140 frustrated vs 9 satisfied** (up from 130/7 last report)
- **133 wrong-approach instances, 45 misunderstood requests**
- **5 commits across 87 sessions** (down from 7/52 — getting worse)
- 8 disaster recovery sessions from Claude-caused damage

### What works

- **Parallel agent audits** — still your best pattern (144 Agent calls)
- **Hook-based enforcement** — the only reliable guardrail mechanism
- **The governance engineering** — skills, CLAUDE.md, hooks. The infrastructure is solid even if Claude doesn't always follow it

### What still fails

Same top 3 as last report, unchanged:

1. **Acting before reading** — Claude ignores plans, context, existing files. Guesses instead of looking.
2. **Unauthorized changes** — writes to wrong files/branches, applies fixes without permission, runs destructive commands
3. **Babysitting loop** — you correct Claude, Claude drifts, you correct again. 100+ minute sessions where errors compound

### What changed since last report

- Hooks are live (destructive git blocker, sensitive data blocker, circuit breaker) — **addressed**
- Skills built (9 co-work skills) — **built but not validated**
- CLAUDE.md slimmed with skill refs — **done**
- Auto-stash hook — **removed** (was destroying in-flight work)
- Slash command discovery — **broken** in VSCode extension, workaround via SessionStart hook injection
- CLAUDE.md not always read — **new problem**, mitigated by hook injection
- Chat sessions disappearing — **new problem**, mitigated by session file logging

### Still unresolved

- Skills not tested on real work
- Governance index not written yet
- Staleness remediation across 5 governance frameworks
- Commit rate still dangerously low
- VSCode extension bugs (slash menu, CLAUDE.md loading, chat loss) — no fix available, only workarounds

### Bottom line

The infrastructure is better. The platform is unreliable. The gap between what you've built and what Claude actually follows in practice is the core problem — and that gap can only close through testing the skills on real threads and iterating when they fail.

## ASSISTANT
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The failure pattern across this session: I built advisory rules and expected them to change behaviour. Advisory rules don't work — that's literally in the memory from the first critical failure. Only mechanical enforcement works.

**What actually worked this session:** Hooks. They're mechanical. The git blocker stops destructive commands. The circuit breaker stops retry loops. No discipline required — the tool physically can't execute.

**What didn't work:** Every skill. They're documents Claude reads and then ignores under pressure. Same failure mode as CLAUDE.md rules.

**The root cause:** Skills are instructions. Instructions require discipline. Claude doesn't have discipline. The only things that change behaviour are constraints that physically prevent the wrong action.

**What I should do now:**

Convert the critical skill behaviours into hooks — mechanical enforcement, not advice:

1. **Anti-drift hook (PreToolUse):** Before any Write/Edit, check if the file being modified relates to the stated thread outcome. If not, inject a warning.
2. **Confirm-before-execute hook (PreToolUse on Write/Edit):** After research/design phase, require the thread to have a confirmed plan before any file writes happen.
3. **Verify-after-build hook (PostToolUse on Write/Edit):** After any MDX/JSX write, auto-run the smoke test.

These would make `/thread`, `/build`, and `/iterate` behaviours mechanical instead of advisory.

The skills stay as reference docs for humans and for Claude's context. But the enforcement moves to hooks.

Want me to build these, or is this session done?
