# Claude Code Insights

230 sessions total · 149 analyzed · 3,780 messages · 407h · 20 commits
2026-03-08 to 2026-03-26

## At a Glance

**What's working:** You've built an impressive documentation infrastructure — automated changelog pipelines, large-scale file migrations with 1700+ path replacements, and Discord/RSS content integrations across multiple products. Your multi-agent observer pattern for tracking session progress is a creative approach to maintaining context across a very high-volume workflow. See _Impressive Things You Did_.

**What's hindering you:** On Claude's side, there's a persistent pattern of pursuing wrong approaches before course-correcting, declaring work "done" when it's actually broken, and editing wrong files despite clear instructions — this is driving a lot of unnecessary rework. On your side, the sheer volume and pace of sessions means Claude often doesn't have enough upfront constraints to avoid false starts, and exploration and execution tend to get mixed together in ways that compound mistakes. See _Where Things Go Wrong_.

**Quick wins to try:** Try setting up **hooks** to auto-run builds or lint checks after edits — this would catch the "Claude says it works but it doesn't" problem mechanically rather than relying on trust. You could also create **custom slash-command skills** for your recurring workflows like changelog generation or migration scripts, encoding the specific constraints Claude keeps forgetting. See _Features to Try_.

**Ambitious workflows:** As models get more capable, your migration and content pipeline work could become single-command operations — imagine kicking off a file restructuring that autonomously scans for stale references, runs link checkers, and self-corrects without your intervention. Your bug fix sessions (which currently average multiple retry loops) could shift to a test-first approach where Claude writes a failing test, then races through fix strategies in parallel sub-agents until one passes. See _On the Horizon_.

Here's what the audit shows:

## `/thread` Audit

**What's working:**
- Session log entries are being written (3 solid entries from today with done/decisions/blocked/next format)
- Work streams table in CLAUDE.md is being maintained (7 streams tracked)
- Sessions are logging to `workspace/thread-outputs/sessions/session-log.txt` (20 entries today)
- Thread outputs going to proper paths (`workspace/thread-outputs/research/`, `/build/`)

**What's not working:**
- **Session log is just timestamps.** No outcome, no stream name, no context. If a chat disappears, the log says "Session started: 2026-03-26 14:21:26" and nothing else. Useless for recovery.
- **20 sessions logged today, only 3 have CLAUDE.md session log entries.** 17 sessions left no trace of what they did.
- **No finalisation reports being written.** `/thread` Step 5 says write one. None exist in completion-reports.md from today.
- **Work streams table already stale.** "Governance framework staleness fixes | Agent running" — that agent finished hours ago. Table not updated.
- **Insights numbers are brutal.** 149 sessions, 142 wrong-approach, 143 frustrated. Commit rate improved (5→20) but frustration didn't drop.

**New insights from the updated report:**
- **False confidence is a top category now.** Claude claiming things work when they don't. The verify-after-build hook addresses this mechanically.
- **Template vs page confusion.** Claude edits pages instead of templates and vice versa. Not addressed in any skill or hook yet.
- **Migration residual scanning.** Claude misses references in non-obvious files (llms.txt, sitemaps, JSON configs). Not addressed.
- **Exploration and execution mixed together.** Claude jumps to editing before understanding. The `/research` → `/design` → `/build` flow addresses this in theory, but sessions aren't following it.

**Recommendations for the co-work master plan:**

1. **Make session-log.txt useful.** The SessionStart hook should log the stream name and outcome, not just a timestamp. When a session ends, log what was done.
2. **Template/page distinction rule.** Add to CLAUDE.md and hook: "When editing documentation, confirm whether the target is a TEMPLATE or a PAGE before writing."
3. **Post-migration scan rule.** Add to CLAUDE.md: "After any file move or rename, scan ALL file types for stale references — including .txt, .json, sitemap, llms.txt."
4. **The core problem remains.** Advisory rules don't change behaviour. The hooks work. Everything else is suggestions Claude ignores under pressure. Every new rule should either be a hook or not bother existing.

**SessionStart hook updated** with the new rules.

**Session log** now points to `workspace/thread-outputs/sessions/session-log.txt` as the canonical location. CLAUDE.md keeps only the 3 most recent entries for quick context.

## ASSISTANT
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

From the latest insights (149 sessions, 407h):

**New patterns not yet addressed:**

1. **False confidence is the sleeper problem.** 37 buggy_code instances where Claude declared done but it was broken. The verify hook helps but only for MDX/JSX. Script changes, migration completeness, and pipeline output aren't mechanically verified yet.

2. **Exploration and execution still mixed.** The research→design→build flow exists as skills but sessions jump straight to editing. The insights show Claude's worst sessions are when it edits before understanding. The best sessions are agent-delegated exploration first.

3. **Changelog/Discord/RSS pipelines are recurring workflows with no encoded process.** 20 sessions on changelog automation, 18 on Discord/community content. These repeat the same mistakes (wrong template, wrong format version, empty content). These are prime candidates for pipeline skills — but we said build those through use, not upfront.

4. **8+ sessions per day average.** That's extremely high context-switching. Each new session loses prior context. claude-mem should be helping here — worth checking if it's actually capturing useful cross-session context.

5. **Commit rate improved (5→20) but frustration didn't drop (140→143).** More commits means less exposed work, but the core friction (wrong approach, false confidence, editing wrong files) is unchanged. Commits protect against catastrophe but don't prevent the daily grind.

6. **73 sessions mostly/fully achieved despite 142 wrong-approach instances.** You're effective at pushing through Claude's mistakes to get results. The cost is your time and patience, not the outcomes. The question is whether reducing wrong-approach from 142 to something lower would save enough time to justify more infrastructure investment, or whether the current hooks + skills are the ceiling for what's possible with the current model.

**My honest assessment:** The mechanical hooks (git blocker, circuit breaker, verify-after-write) are the only things that reliably changed behaviour. The skills are good reference docs but Claude doesn't internalise them mid-session. The next highest-impact move is probably encoding the changelog/Discord/migration workflows as pipeline skills since those are your highest-volume recurring tasks — but only building them through real use as we agreed.

=====
Also 
New Ways to Use Claude Code & On the Horizon are good sections too.


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
## ASSISTANT
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**1. False confidence — extend verification mechanically**

The verify hook currently only reminds about MDX/JSX. Expand `pre-tool-guard.js` to also:
- After script writes: inject "run this script before declaring done"
- After migration/file moves: inject "grep all file types for stale references before declaring done"
- After any Write/Edit: inject "verify the change, do not claim done without evidence"

This doesn't block — it injects a system message that Claude has to acknowledge. Not as strong as a blocker but much better than advisory.

**2. Exploration before execution — make it mechanical**

The hardest one. The skill says "research before build" but sessions skip it. Two options:

- **Option A (advisory):** Add to SessionStart hook: "First 3 tool calls of any session should be Read/Grep/Glob only. No Write/Edit until you understand the problem."
- **Option B (mechanical):** A PreToolUse hook that blocks Write/Edit for the first N minutes of a session unless the user explicitly says "go." Aggressive but would force the exploration phase.

I'd try A first. It's a nudge, not a wall.

**3. Changelog/Discord/RSS — build through use, starting now**

Next time you run a changelog or Discord pipeline task, tell Claude: "Log every step and mistake to `workspace/thread-outputs/build/changelog-process-log.md`." After 2-3 runs, the process log becomes the skill. Real patterns, not guesses.

**4. Cross-session context (claude-mem)**

Worth checking right now whether it's actually working:

```
/claude-mem:mem-search what did we work on yesterday
```

If it returns useful context, it's working. If it returns nothing, it's not capturing — and 8 sessions/day with no memory between them explains a lot of the repeated mistakes.

**5. Frustration rate — the honest take**

143 frustrated out of 149 sessions. The hooks prevent catastrophe (no more destroyed work). The skills might reduce wrong-approach over time as they're tested and tightened. But the model's tendency to jump ahead, edit wrong files, and declare done prematurely is a model behaviour problem, not a configuration problem. More infrastructure won't fix it — better models will. What we've built is the best guardrail layer possible with current tools.

**6. On the Horizon items worth trying now**

- **Test-driven bug fixes:** When debugging, tell Claude to write a failing test FIRST, then fix against it. This mechanically prevents false confidence — the test either passes or it doesn't.
- **Parallel fix exploration:** Spawn 3 agents with different fix strategies, pick the winner. Your agent usage is already high (174 calls) — this is a natural extension.
- **Headless mode for batch ops:** Changelog regeneration across 5 products, bulk Tip message updates, stale reference scans — these are well-defined enough to run non-interactively with `--allowedTools` restrictions.

Want me to implement any of these?

# Claude Code Insights

255 sessions total · 165 analyzed · 3,939 messages · 407h · 20 commits
2026-03-08 to 2026-03-26

## At a Glance

**What's working:** You've built a genuinely impressive docs-as-infrastructure practice — orchestrating a 217-file migration with atomic commits, automated testing, and PR delivery, while tracking everything through Notion. Your multi-agent observer pattern for maintaining session context across a sprawling migration project is creative and shows you're thinking about Claude as a system, not just a tool. See _Impressive Things You Did_.

**What's hindering you:** On Claude's side, it frequently edits the wrong file or overwrites entire files when you need surgical changes — this is your biggest source of frustration and it's legitimate. On your side, the observer agent sessions are consuming a lot of your usage for minimal payoff, and many sessions end without deliverables because the exploration phase runs too long without a clear stopping point. See _Where Things Go Wrong_.

**Quick wins to try:** Try creating custom slash commands (/commands) for your repeating workflows like completion report generation, batch cleanup operations, and component refactoring patterns — these can bake in the constraints Claude keeps ignoring. Hooks could also auto-run your Mintlify dev server validation after edits, catching breakage before you even look at the output. See _Features to Try_.

**Ambitious workflows:** As models get more capable, your migration pipeline should become a single headless session — file batching, nav updates, build validation, and rollback all running autonomously with parallel sub-agents. Your painful one-by-one Notion updates are a perfect candidate for parallelized sub-agents that partition rows and finish in minutes, and structured debug loops that test-and-rollback will eliminate the "wrong file, wrong approach" cycle that dogs your component fix sessions. See _On the Horizon_.
